17:19:46","updated":"2021-07-07 09:04:51","type":"photo","message":"“In 1997, a little after I moved to the USA, I met the mother of a Tamilian friend. I could not communicate with her, except for greeting her with folded hands, because she did not speak any Hindi or English, and I did not speak any Tamil. That incident made me realize the importance of having a common language to communicate, and ignited in me the drive to promote Hindi through theater. In 2006, I presented a small skit at a function for the Senior Citizens Group in Atlanta which was well received. This led me to think of having a theater group of our own. Theater is powerful medium of self expression and life is a game of ups and downs (Dhoop & Chaoon). In the 10 years since the inception of the group, we have been able to create our own identity in our community. We have reached a stage, where, for the audition of the Bollywood movie Simran, 90 % of our members were present. I am my own inspiration. I write most of my plays/skits on subjects like social problems, communal harmony, immigration, entertainment etc, each with a powerful message. It is very challenging doing theater. It is driven by passion, and without any earnings. There are times when I wonder why I am doing this! When we have a show, for four months, this is all I do, day in and day out. Coordination can be very tiring and affect your daily routine drastically. After each show, I think this is the last one. But after a few months, I start all over again with new vigor. Finance has always been the biggest hurdle in doing our shows. Even with a nominal ticket price of $10, not many people attend. This hurts me a lot. South Asians contribute generously to religious establishments and are always ready to pay top dollars to view performances by Bollywood artists. These people should support people like us who present healthy entertainment for everyone. We keep a donation box during the show, but it mostly remains empty. We spend our own money to do our shows. But I will not stop and I will not tire. I am a very stubborn person. We started from ground zero. With continuous hard work, we have come this far. The lines from Rabindranath Tagore’s poem keep echoing in my ears. “If no one answers your call, then walk alone, walk alone my friend”. – Sandhya Bhagat Sandhya Bhagat is the founder of Dhoop Chaaon theater group and Natkhat Rangshala, a Hindi theater school for children. She is co-founder of Hindi-Urdu Sanjhe Bol, a platform for poets of the two languages. She is also a co-founder of Dhoop-Chaaon, a Hindi short film production company which has produced two films so far- “Natkhat Rangeelay” and “Ye Aurtein bhee kya bla hain”. Bhagat is supported in her endeavors by her husband Anil Bhagat and two sons, Gandharv and Kartikay. #IndiansofAtlanta - Food Cookout in Atlanta, by Atlanta Tamil Makkal 2017 has been one terrific and exciting year for most of us so far, we saw history being made - youngsters rewrote the fate and made us believe anything is possible if there is strong will - with universally acclaimed peaceful Jallikattu Protests. For all of us living away from home - it was agonizing to watch and feel that we couldn’t be part of it, physically present in Tamil Nadu but still we showed our support in whatever forms we could. Most of us didn’t want to stop there but try to make a difference in any way we can. When thinking how can women who live across the globe contribute to our community - an idea sparked. The idea was to organize a small cookout with friends and families where home made food can be sold for a price and all proceeds can be used to support a social cause. The idea quickly caught interest of few like-minded, self-motivated women who started with planning immediately. But then we needed a theme and some kind of attraction to generate the interests in people and make them want to come. Since we decided to support Lake Restoration Efforts lead by Piyush Manush, a well known environmentalist in Salem, who also is part of Salem Citizens Forum, the theme became “Go-Green”. We still needed the event attractions. Of late there has been growing awareness and interest among us in trying Traditional Food, so we decided to cook Traditional Food and introduce Traditional Games to the children - the very games that we adults have played in our 80’s, 90’s. We sought help from other friends and their friends and quickly the word spread and more people showed interest. We used divide and conquer strategy - Cooking Team involved finding volunteers and brain storm menu options, and allocating work, Marketing Team - Creating fliers, posting in whatsapp group, Facebook and such, Sports Team - Planning group games which are safe enough for kids, props arrangements and organizing, Logistics team - location scouting, getting park permits, finding the materials needed from A-Z for that day. Each team worked on its own brainstorming but we still gathered on conference call or whatsapp to share information and always took decisions collectively. Food: Lot of varieties to choose from, selecting the menu was one of the toughest part of this project. when we floated the idea of all traditional food menu, we were surprised to hear most haven’t even heard of such dishes, so we decided to keep a mix of traditional and modern day options and mainly kids friendly. Since the event time was 4-7, we decided to pick menu that is good for snacking. As soon as we sent the flier out, many women and men came forward to cook. For the event, the cooking team made 300+ idli, 200 vadai, 4 trays of Kesari, 5 trays of sambar, few trays of various chutneys, 10’s lbs of Muruku, 10’s lbs of Sweet Boondhi, over 600 Sweet paniyaaram, Over 400 Kaara paniyaaram more than 25 ltrs of Koozhu, 10 ltrs of Panagam, more than 30 ltrs of Lemonade, Neer Moru, 10 ltrs of Mango Lassi, over 350 Dosas. We ensured the prices were nominal, all foods were priced less than $6. Adults, Kids were excited to try both traditional food like Koozhu and also Live Dosai with many varieties to choose from Plain, Murungai Keerai Dosai, Millets Dosai, Masala Dosai, Oothappam. Snacks were a great hit - Badam Sweet, Murukkus, Poli, Boondhi and many more. Games: When we decided on traditional games we were not sure how interesting it could be for the kids of this generation since most were born here and haven’t had chance to play such games. But to our surprise the kids loved to play them name a few - Kulakulaya Munthirika, Poo Parikka Varukirom, 7 Kal, Oru Kudam Thanni Oothi. Adults also went back to reminisce their childhood days. We also arranged \"show and tell” about the games like Thayam, Aadupuli, Pallanguli, Goli, Pambaram and Undigoal. It was such a pleasure to see the kids wanting to know and gets their hands on and try them! Pambaram and Pallanguli were the most sought after games! It was such a treat and sweet surprise to see men and women shed their inhibitions and start playing with the kids. Women were fascinated about Poo Parika Varukirom, Men had a gala time playing Kabadi and wouldn’t stop playing! We completed with a grand finale with all the ladies and kids joining the Kummi dance. No Plastic: To stay true to the fund raising cause and the event being on Earth Day, we stuck to \"Reduce Waste, No Plastic” vision. We made some drastic and some can even call bold decisions - Encourage everyone eat by hand like we usually do at home, Reuse compostable plates - Guests could bring the same plate they were eating to earn green tokens, 3 of which will give $1 token for next food purchase, provide free tap water apart from bottled water, insist volunteers (truncated)","postUrl":"https://www.facebook.com/groups/862281510551753/permalink/1265427500237150","subscriberCount":0,"score":1.6842105263157894,"statistics":{"actual":{"likeCount":25,"shareCount":3,"commentCount":3,"loveCount":1,"wowCount":0,"hahaCount":0,"sadCount":0,"angryCount":0,"thankfulCount":0,"careCount":0},"expected":{"likeCount":2,"shareCount":2,"commentCount":3,"loveCount":2,"wowCount":0,"hahaCount":0,"sadCount":1,"angryCount":0,"thankfulCount":0,"careCount":0}},"account":{"id":7865493,"name":"Atlanta Tamil Makkal (ATM)","profileImage":"https://scontent-sea1-1.xx.fbcdn.net/v/t31.18172-8/cp0/c42.0.50.50a/p50x50/18491637_10154713953793230_4762884173072444583_o.jpg?_nc_cat=108&ccb=1-5&_nc_sid=ac9ee4&_nc_ohc=T4bohSNkEIAAX83h-I2&_nc_ht=scontent-sea1-1.xx&oh=00_AT-_YwTLB_5rbu7BjceLeoE16X5yE10NqlyUODv0BBHFVA&oe=61FCFC7F","subscriberCount":3610,"url":"https://www.facebook.com/groups/862281510551753","platform":"Facebook","platformId":"862281510551753","accountType":"facebook_group","pageCategory":"none","verified":false},"languageCode":"en","legacyId":0,"id":"7865493|1265427500237150"},{"platformId":"160209324036106_1426043147452711","platform":"Facebook","date":"2017-04-27 10:52:34","updated":"2021-08-13 08:38:12","type":"native_video","description":"Hare Krishna! premieres in June at the Illuminate Film Festival before a national theatrical rollout later in the month.
